## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (continuous-time growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as an ODE in time t and population size P. Classical population ecology expresses dP_dt as P times a per-capita growth term that may depend on density (P) and/or time (t) to capture density dependence, carrying capacity limits, Allee effects, harvesting, and seasonality.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net inflow/outflow independent of P)
- Power-law (generalized mass-action) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (super-/sub-linear growth; aggregation or interference effects)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slow trend in per-capita growth due to environment/management)
- Seasonally forced per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting birth/death rates)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (with c1 < 0 gives carrying-capacity limitation)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (per-capita growth decreases ~log with size; asymmetric approach to capacity)
- Richards-type logistic (alternative parameterization): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized sigmoid approach to an upper bound)
- Allee effect (strong) model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (negative growth below threshold c1; density limitation via c2 < 0)
- Saturating/limited recruitment term: dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) - c2 * P (birth term saturates at high P, with linear mortality)
- Harvesting/exploitation with refuge-like saturation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (density dependence plus saturating removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Factor P in dP_dt → guarantees extinction boundary at P = 0 and interpretable per-capita rate (dP_dt / P).
- Linear decrease of per-capita growth with P (i.e., dP_dt/P ≈ c0 + c1*P) → classic crowding/resource limitation leading to a carrying capacity.
- Logarithmic dependence log(c1/(P+c2)) in the per-capita term → Gompertz-like dynamics with slower approach to the upper bound and asymmetry around the inflection.
- Presence of (P - c1) factor → Allee threshold: sign change in growth at low P indicating mate limitation/cooperation effects.
- Exponent on P inside the density term (e.g., P**c2) → tunable strength/shape of density dependence; c2 > 1 sharpens regulation, 0 < c2 < 1 softens it.
- Additive constant term in dP_dt → external inputs/outputs (stocking, migration) that can sustain P even when P is small.
- Sinusoidal time modulation in coefficients → seasonal forcing that produces periodic variation in growth, potentially inducing cycles in P.
- Subtractive term proportional to P (−c*P) alongside a saturating gain term → separable birth and death processes with limited recruitment and density-independent mortality.
- Saturating removal term P/(P+c) → harvesting/predation limited by effort/handling, preventing removal from scaling indefinitely with P.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG16)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6 + c7*P
Candidate formulas: 53

GT is a fixed function of **P only** (no dependence on *t*):
\[
0.86778\,(-1+P/6.0579)(1-P/14.1851)P \;+\;0.86778\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.86778\,P.
\]
Expand the cubic part:
\[
(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P = -P + P^2\Big(\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b\Big) - \tfrac{1}{ab}P^3,
\]
so GT has the form
\[
\alpha P^{1/3} \;+\; A_1 P \;+\; A_2 P^2 \;+\; A_3 P^3
\]
with **nonzero** coefficients for \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2, P^3\). In particular, it is a smooth polynomial-in-P plus \(P^{1/3}\), with **no Max/hinge, no rational term, no log/exp/sin**, and no piecewise behavior.

Below, each candidate is checked for whether it can be reduced (by choosing its free constants) to exactly \(\alpha P^{1/3}+A_1P+A_2P^2+A_3P^3\) for **all real P**.

---

### 1
Contains \(P^2\cdot \max(0,P+c_1)\) and \(P\cdot \max(0,P+c_7)\): these are piecewise (hinge) terms. To avoid piecewise behavior for all real P, their coefficients must be 0 (set \(c_0=0\) and \(c_6=0\)), but then no \(P^3\) term can be produced. Also has a rational \(P*c_2/(P^{c_3}+c_4)\) which cannot become a polynomial for all P unless \(c_2=0\). Then only linear \(P*c_5\) remains (plus possible \(e^{c_9 t}\) which must be killed by \(c_8=0\)). Missing \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **No match.**

### 2
Has \(P^{1/3}c_0\) (good), but also hinge terms \(P^2 c_1\max(0,P+c_2)\) and \(P c_4\max(0,P+c_5)\) which must be zeroed to avoid piecewise behavior (set \(c_1=0,c_4=0\)), and an exponential-in-t term \(P^{c_6}c_7 e^{c_8 t}\) which must be removed (set \(c_7=0\) or \(c_8=0\) and then still \(P^{c_6}\) would remain unless \(c_7=0\)). After removing those, only \(P^{1/3}\), \(P\), constant remain—no \(P^2,P^3\). **No match.**

### 3
Form \(c_0P^{1/3}+c_1P^3+c_2P^2\). Missing linear \(P\) term (GT has nonzero \(P\) coefficient). Cannot generate \(P\). **No match.**

### 4
Same as (3): \(P^{1/3}\) + \(P^3\) + \(P^2\) (two \(P^2\) coefficients combine). Still no \(P\). **No match.**

### 5
Has \(P^{1/3}\) plus hinge terms \(P^2 c_1\max(0,P+c_2)\) and \(P c_3\max(0,P)\) and constant. To avoid piecewise for all real P, must set \(c_1=0\) and \(c_3=0\), leaving only \(P^{1/3}\)+constant. Missing \(P,P^2,P^3\). **No match.**

### 6
Has \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^3\), \(P^2\) terms, plus a hinge \(c_4\max(0,-P+c_5)\) which must be removed (set \(c_4=0\)). Still no linear \(P\). **No match.**

### 7
Has \(P^3\), \(P^2\), \(P\), and \(P^{c_4}\) plus a hinge. You could set hinge coefficient \(c_6=0\) and set \(c_4=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Then the structure becomes
\[
c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_5P^{1/3},
\]
which matches GT’s required monomials exactly. So **this candidate can match** by choosing constants to equal GT coefficients:
- set \(c_4=1/3\),
- set \(c_6=0\),
- choose \(c_5=\alpha=0.8677806610632854\),
- choose \(c_3=A_1\), \(c_1+c_2=A_2\), \(c_0=A_3\) (any split of \(A_2\) across \(c_1,c_2\) works).

Therefore **Candidate 7 matches GT**.

### 8
Has \(P^{1/3}\) but includes hinge terms \(P^2 c_1\max(0,P)\) and \(P c_3\max(0,P+c_4)\). To avoid piecewise globally, must set \(c_1=0,c_3=0\), leaving \(P^{1/3}+P+\)constant. Missing \(P^2,P^3\). **No match.**

### 9
Hinge terms again; removing them kills higher powers. Also has a fixed \(+P\) (coefficient 1) which would force GT’s linear coefficient to be 1, but GT’s linear coefficient is not 1 (it is \(0.86778\) plus contribution from cubic expansion). Even before that, cannot create \(P^3\) without hinge. **No match.**

### 10
Same hinge issue; removing hinge removes \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 11
Same hinge issue; removing hinge removes \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 12
Has \(P^{1/3}\), a hinge-generated \(P^3\) term (via \(P^2\max(0,P+c_2)\)) which is piecewise unless coefficient is 0. If keep it, function is not globally polynomial; if remove it, no \(P^3\). Also only \(P^2\) and \(P\) otherwise. **No match.**

### 13
Same hinge dependence for \(P^3\); cannot be globally equal to smooth GT. **No match.**

### 14
No \(P^{1/3}\) unless set \(c_3=-2/3\) in \(P*P^{c_3}c_4=c_4P^{1+c_3}\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). That part is possible. But also includes hinge \(c_7\max(0,-P+c_8)\) which must be removed (set \(c_7=0\)). Then expression becomes polynomial terms plus \(P^{1/3}\) and extra linear terms \(P*c5+P*c6\). This can match GT (since linear coefficients can be adjusted). Also has two separate \(P^2\) terms (fine). So **Candidate 14 can also match** by:
- set \(c_7=0\),
- set \(c_3=-2/3\) and \(c_4=\alpha\),
- choose \(c_0,c_1,c_2,c_5,c_6\) to match \(P^3,P^2,P\) coefficients.

Thus **Candidate 14 matches GT**.

### 15
Has \(P*c3*(P*c4)^{c5} = c3*c4^{c5} P^{1+c5}\). Can set \(c5=-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Remove hinge by \(c_8=0\). Remaining terms include \(P^3,P^2,P\) and \(P^{1/3}\). Coefficients are freely adjustable. **Matches GT**.

### 16
Has hinge terms \(P^2\max(0,P+c_1)\) and \(P*c5\max(0,P+c_6)\). To avoid piecewise, must set their coefficients 0, killing any \(P^3\) source. Remaining terms are \(P^{1+c2}\) and linear terms only; cannot get both \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) simultaneously without hinge. **No match.**

### 17
Has \(P^{1/3}\) but also hinge terms and an \(e^{P c_7}\) term. Must set \(c_6=0\) to remove exponential-in-P; must set hinge coefficients to 0 to avoid piecewise, which removes \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 18
Pure sum of monomials \(P^2\), \(P\), and two power terms \(P^{c_4},P^{c_6}\). No \(P^3\) unless set one exponent to 3; no \(P^{1/3}\) unless set one exponent to 1/3. But then you still need \(P^3,P^2,P\) and \(P^{1/3}\): you can set \(c_4=3\) and \(c_6=1/3\) (or vice versa), and use \(P^2 c_0\) and linear combination \(P(c_1+c_2+c_3)\). Coefficients adjustable. **Matches GT**.

### 19
Contains hinge terms and a rational term \(P*c_3/(P^{c_4}+c_5)\). To match a polynomial for all P, must zero out rational term (\(c_3=0\)) and hinge terms (\(c_0=0,c_7=0\)), leaving only \(P^2\) and linear terms—no \(P^{1/3}\) and no \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 20
Has \(P^{1/3}\) and a free \(P^{c_6}\) term (can set \(c_6=2\) or 3), but \(P^3\) would have to come from hinge term \(P^2\max(0,P+c_2)\), which is piecewise unless removed. If removed, no \(P^3\). If kept, not equal to smooth GT. **No match.**

### 21–27
All are built from hinge terms plus a rational term \(P*c_2/(P^{c_3}+c_4)\) and linear pieces. To equal GT (smooth polynomial + \(P^{1/3}\)) for all real P:
- hinge terms must be removed (coefficients 0) to avoid piecewise behavior,
- rational term must be removed (numerator coefficient 0) to avoid non-polynomial behavior.
After doing so, only linear terms remain (sometimes plus \(P\) fixed). No way to produce \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\). **No match for 21–27.**

### 28
Has \(P^{1/3}\). But \(P^3\) again only via hinge \(P*c6\max(0,P+c_7)\) (piecewise) unless you set \(c_6=0\), losing \(P^3\). Other power term \(P*P^{c_3}c_4\) can create \(P^3\) by \(c_3=2\), and can create \(P^2\) by \(c_3=1\), but only one exponent available there. You do have a hinge term too, but cannot keep it. So you cannot get both \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) smoothly along with \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P\). **No match.**

### 29–30
Include hinge terms; 29 also has log. To match polynomial, log must be removed (set its coefficient 0) and hinge removed (set hinge coefficients 0), leaving only linear + one power term \(P^{c_5}\). Cannot get both \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) and \(P^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 31
Has \(P^{1/3}\) but includes hinge and a rational \(P*c_3/(P+c_4)\) which cannot be polynomial for all P unless \(c_3=0\). Removing hinge removes \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 32–33
Contain hinge terms and logs; must remove logs and hinges, losing \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 34–35
No \(P^{1/3}\) term (only \(P^{1+c_2}\) etc.). Could set \(c_2=-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\), but then need \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) too: only one additional power term available (in 34) plus hinge term which must be removed to avoid piecewise. 35 adds log which must be removed. Cannot get all required monomials smoothly. **No match.**

### 36
Has \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P^2\) (explicit) and linear terms, but \(P^3\) only via hinge \(P*c5\max(0,P+c_6)\) which must be removed for smoothness. **No match.**

### 37
Has \(P^{1/3}\) and hinge term; also has rational \(P*c_6/(P+c_7)\) which must be removed (set \(c_6=0\)) to be polynomial. Removing hinge removes \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 38–39
No \(P^{1/3}\) unless set \(c_8=1/3\) in \(P^{c_8}c_9\), but then still need \(P^3\) and \(P^2\). \(P^3\) only via hinge \(P^2\max(0,P+c_1)\) which cannot be kept. Also rational term in 38/39 must be removed. **No match.**

### 40
Has \(P^{1/3}\) but includes hinge and a non-polynomial fraction \(P*P^{c_3}c_4/(P^{c_3}+c_5)\) which cannot equal a polynomial for all P unless set \(c_4=0\). Then again \(P^3\) only via hinge. **No match.**

### 41
Has \(P^{1/3}\) and hinge plus a log(exp()) term; must remove log term (set \(c_7=0\)) and hinge (set \(c_4=0\)), losing \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 42–43
Contain hinge and exp(P*...). Must remove exp term (set its coefficient 0) and hinge (set hinge coefficients 0), losing \(P^3\) and \(P^{1/3}\). **No match.**

### 44
Has \(P^{1/3}\) and hinge plus sin(P...). Must remove sin term (set coefficient 0) and hinge (set hinge coefficients 0), losing \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 45
Has log(c9*t+1) depending on t; GT has no t dependence, so must set its coefficient \(c_8=0\). Remaining is like candidate 18: \(P^2\), linear terms, and two power terms. As with 18, can set one exponent to 3 and the other to 1/3, and adjust coefficients to match. **Matches GT**.

### 46
No \(P^{1/3}\) unless set \(c_2=-2/3\) in \(P*P^{c_2}=P^{1/3}\). But then need \(P^2\) and \(P^3\): you have \(P*P^{c_3}c_4\) can make either \(P^2\) or \(P^3\) but not both, and hinge term would be needed for the other but cannot be kept. **No match.**

### 47
Has t-dependent log; must set its coefficient \(c_6=0\). Then reduces to same hinge-based structure as others; removing hinge removes \(P^3\). **No match.**

### 48
